This becomes evident when one examines actin - labelled host cells infected with the bacteria under the microscope . In these cells , one will observe slender and long actin enriched structures attached directly behind the bacterial cell 535 – 537 , 568 . These structures , commonly referred to as comet ( or rocket ) tails , provide the propulsive forces necessary to move the bacteria within the host cytosol ( Figure 1 . 12 ) 474 , 493 , 494 . When comet / rocket tails push the bacteria towards the host plasma membrane , the bacteria begin to generate an actin - rich membrane protrusion which eventually propels the bacteria directly into nearby cells 115 , 249 , 493 , 534 . In this section I will outline the major bacterial and host components that control comet / rocket tail growth and motility . L . monocytogenes ActA The major ( and sole ) determinant of comet / rocket tail formation is the L . monocytogenes effector protein ActA 67 , 518 , 569 – 572 . L . monocytogenes mutants that are deleted for the ActA gene ( actA ) can enter the host cytosol but do not recruit actin nor generate comet / rocket tails and thus are immotile 67 , 535 . Further support of this was shown through the covalent attachment of purified ActA onto small ( 0 . 5 - 2 µm ) polystyrene beads that when incubated in an actin - rich cytoplasmic extract , resulted in the formation of a motile comet / rocket tail at the surface of each bead 572 . 30 Structurally , L . monocytogenes ActA contains three major domains . A relatively hydrophobic C - terminal region anchors ActA into the bacterial membrane 573 . The two remaining domains , exposed to the host cytosol , are involved in the bacterial actin - based motility mechanism 67 , 573 . An N - terminal acidic domain followed by a central proline - rich region activate and regulate Arp2 / 3 activity at the bacterial cell surface 105 , 574 , 575 . The N - terminal domain directly binds to the Arp2 / 3 complex as well as G - actin 105 . Crucially , the N - terminal domain functions as a bona fide NPF / activator of the Arp2 / 3 complex , and thus , by itself is sufficient to induce motility 575 . In fact , it was the ground - breaking study by Welch and colleagues which demonstrated L . monocytogenes ActA as the first activator of Arp2 / 3 52 . When purified Arp2 / 3 was incubated with fluorescently - tagged actin and L . monocytogenes bacteria , actin filaments accumulated as a “cloud” around individual bacterial cells 52 . On rare instances , short comet tails were observed in preparations using the purified Arp2 / 3 52 . Structurally , the N - terminal region of ActA possess sequence similarly to the host NPF N - WASp 573 . The central proline - rich region of ActA is dispensable for bacterial motility 573 . Functionally , this region of ActA binds to VASP and likely makes actin - based motility efficient 573 , 576 . VASP binding to profilin could function to accelerate filament elongation of the comet / rocket tail 219 , 573 . Alternatively , VASP could stabilize actin filaments within the growing comet / rocket tail via its actin - bundling activity 219 . The L . monocytogenes actin comet / rocket tail Once inside the host cell cytosol , L . monocytogenes bacteria upregulate ActA expression 570 . Following successive rounds of replication , ActA becomes highly expressed at one pole of the bacterial cell 518 , 519 . In fact , this asymmetrical distribution of ActA is essential for unidirectional actin - based motility as biomimetic studies show defective ActA - coated bead motility when the ActA molecules are attached symmetrically about the bead 572 . Arp2 / 3 complexes that are recruited and activated at the bacterial cell surface ultimately generate a long slender branched actin - containing comet / rocket tail ( Figure 1 . 12 ) 52 , 105 , 474 , 520 . However , despite high levels of Arp2 / 3 within the structures , the comet / rocket tail also contains some long unbranched actin filaments 113 , 114 . Overall , the L . monocytogenes comet / rocket tail , like the eukaryotic lamellipodium and filopodium , depends on the cooperative efforts of an assortment of host proteins for its proper 31 formation and function 474 , 479 , 520 , 573 . Several actin - associated proteins normally involved in the “treadmilling” model of actin polymerization are recruited to comet / rocket tails . These proteins : profilin , ADF / cofilin , the capping protein CapZ , and VASP , are suggested to enhance overall motility rates ( Figure 1 . 12 ) 474 , 479 , 520 . Various F - actin crosslinkers and bundlers have also been immunolocalized to comet / rocket tails , including  - actinin , nexilin , fascin , fimbrin , filamin , and SM22 ( Figure 1 . 12 ) 114 , 115 , 535 , 536 . Inhibition of these proteins results in diverse phenotypic differences such as shorter , slower or even twisted comet tails 114 , 535 , 536 , 577 , 578 . These findings highlight the necessity for a certain degree of stiffness and stability within the structures which is endowed by these F - actin crosslinkers / bundlers 113 . Interestingly , the clathrin coated pit scission protein , dynamin2 , possess actin bundling and nucleating activity 579 . Experiments by Lee and De Camilli uncovered dynamin2 as another crucial component of the comet / rocket tail 579 . In cells expressing a mutant variant of dynamin2 , comets formation and motility rates are reduced 579 . Other host cytoskeletal elements , as well as other filament - forming proteins , are also hijacked by L . monocytogenes during their intracellular motility . Tubulin and the microtubule regulator stathmin have recently been immunolocalized to comet / rocket tails 580 . Depletion of stathmin results in comet / rocket tails that are longer , but oddly , move at slower rates 580 . Components of the spectrin cytoskeleton , such as spectrin and protein 4 . 1 , are recruited to the initial stages of comet / rocket tail formation , and in some instances even prior to actin cloud formation 537 . Interestingly , once comet / rocket tails have formed and elongated in length , these spectrin components appear to shed from the structures 537 . The septin family of proteins are a group of GTP - binding proteins that can oligomerize into filaments 581 . Mostowy and colleagues have demonstrated that SEPT2 and SEPT9 can polymerize into ring - like arrays at comet / rocket tails and around the bacterial cell body ; however , motility rates are not altered in the absence of these proteins 582 . ActA - mediated autophagy avoidance The L . monocytogenes comet / rocket tail is vital for the eventual cell - to - cell spreading of bacteria in vivo as well as during cell culture infections 493 . However , another crucial role for the actin - based motility of L . monocytogenes bacteria is autophagy avoidance 583 , 584 . Autophagy targets defective proteins , damaged organelles as well as bacteria for degradation and thus represents a crucial intracellular mechanism to facilitate 32 immunological function 585 . Yoshikawa and colleagues reveal that ActA - mediated recruitment of the host actin polymerization machinery to the bacterial cell surface functions as a way to cloak the bacteria ( and its surface proteins ) from autophagic recognition 583 , 584 . L . monocytogenes bacteria that express a mutant form of ActA that does not recruit the Arp2 / 3 complex , G - actin and VASP fail to avoid host cell autophagy programs 583 . 1 . 8 . 4 . Membrane protrusion formation As mentioned above , when motile L . monocytogenes bacteria reach the host plasma membrane , they often push against it , forming a finger - like protrusion that is sheathed by plasma membrane ( Figure 1 . 13 ) 493 . This membrane protrusion encloses the bacterial cell at its tip along with its attached actin - rich comet / rocket . The L . monocytogenes - containing membrane protrusion pushes directly into the surface of surrounding host cells ( Figure 1 . 14 ) 493 . The host cell receiving the projecting membrane protrusion generates a large endocytic - like invagination at its surface in order to engulf the structure . Whether or not the host endocytic machinery is at play during membrane protrusion engulfment remains a longstanding question in the field . Following membrane protrusion engulfment , the L . monocytogenes bacteria reside within a double - membraned vacuole which is eventually broken by secreted bacterial pore - forming toxins 477 . Once inside the cytosol of the newly infected host , the bacteria are once again free to generate the actin comet / rocket tail . Compared to the comet / rocket tail , few studies exist which examine the molecular mechanism underlying L . monocytogenes membrane protrusion formation . Two well - known host components which localize specifically to the membrane protrusion are ezrin and the formins 249 , 534 . Interestingly , certain comet / rocket tail proteins , such as α - actinin 1 , are shed immediately prior to membrane protrusion formation 115 . This interplay between protein recruitment and release at the membrane protrusion suggests a potential alteration to the underlying actin network contained with the structures . Indeed , ultrastructural examination of L . monocytogenes reveals long parallel bundles of F - actin with gradually reduced branching of actin towards the base of the structures 113 , 115 , 539 . The presence of these parallel F - actin arrays can be strongly attributed to ezrin and formin proteins within the structures 249 , 534 . Depletion or inhibition of these proteins results in fewer and shorter membrane protrusion , and consequently , diminished bacterial cell - to - cell spreading 249 , 534 . 33 Closer examination of the membrane protrusions generated in cells depleted of ezrin shows that they are structurally perturbed 249 . These findings highlight a crucial role in the switch from branched actin to parallel F - actin arrays in addition to the linkage of these arrays directly to the plasma membrane . Two secreted bacterial factors are also well - established as promoting efficient bacterial dissemination , Internalin C ( InlC ) and Internalin P ( Inl ) 495 , 586 . Rajabian and colleagues demonstrate that Inl C binding to the host adaptor protein Tuba , inhibits normal N - WASp - Tuba interactions 586 . As N - WSAP and Tuba are normally involved in maintaining junction integrity , secretion of InlC results in apical junction tension switching from taut to slack 586 , 587 . Induction of slack apical junctions allows motile L . monocytogenes bacteria to easily deform the host plasma membrane during membrane protrusion formation 586 . In addition to spreading within a layer of cells , such as the intestinal epithelia , L . monocytogenes bacteria also target the basal face of cells ( perpendicular to the monolayer ) in order to gain access to the underlying tissue 495 . To accomplish this , L . monocytogenes bacteria rely on the secreted effector InlP 495 . Specifically , Faralla and colleagues demonstrated an InlP - mediated inhibition of the host junctional protein , afadin , thus leading to a reduction in overall monolayer tractional forces 495 . Faralla and colleagues go on to hypothesize that it is this ability of L . monocytogenes to disrupt cell - substrate interactions that promotes bacterial spread vertically into tissue , such as the fetal stroma , during infections of pregnant women 495 . Following membrane protrusion engulfment , the bacteria reside within double - membranous vacuoles . To escape this structure , L . monocytogenes secrete LLO along with phospholipases A and B 477 . However , recent advances in the field reveal a sub - population of L . monocytogenes bacteria that persistently remain within vacuoles following their cell - to - cell spreading 515 . 1 . 9 . Other relevant actin - hijacking pathogens As mentioned earlier in the introduction of this thesis , several other bacterial pathogens have evolved elegant mechanisms by which to subvert the host actin cytoskeleton during infections . In this section , I will review three members of the Enterobacteriaceae family of Gram - negative bacteria , EPEC , S . Typhimurium and S . 34 flexneri . These pathogens rely on a complex needle - like apparatus , called the Type 3 secretion system ( T3SS ) , to inject potent effector proteins into host cell and thus cause disease 588 – 591 . Additionally , like the L . monocytogenes ActA protein , these bacteria also express on their surface crucial effector proteins 591 , 592 . The T3SS , in conjunction with surface expressed effector proteins , allow each of these bacteria to exploit the actin cytoskeleton at various stages of their infection ( Figures 1 . 15 - 1 . 18 ) 588 – 592 . Furthermore , while there exists extensive literature describing the entire infectious cycle of these pathogens , for the purpose of this thesis , I will be focussing primarily on the actin - rich structures they generate and the molecular mechanisms underlying their formation . 1 . 9 . 1 . Enteropathogenic Escherichia coli ( EPEC ) During EPEC infections these bacteria remain extracellular but are firmly attached to the surface of the host cell 588 , 592 – 594 . The major mechanism by which EPEC tightly associate with the host surface is through their formation of actin - rich pedestals ( Figure 1 . 15 ) 592 , 595 . To accomplish this , EPEC induces actin filament polymerization against the cytosolic leaflet of the host plasma membrane at the site of bacteria - host contact 594 . The polymerization of actin filaments eventually distends the host membrane , raising the bacteria off the natural surface of the host , thus resulting in pedestal formation 588 , 592 ( Fig 1 . 15 ) . Importantly , EPEC pedestals are motile structures and thus allow the bacteria to “surf” atop the surface of the host cell and even spread onto the surface of other nearby cells 596 , 597 . Pedestal formation is initiated following the T3SS - mediated injection of the EPEC effector Tir , which then inserts itself into the host plasma membrane 593 . Tir is the natural ligand of another EPEC effector protein , intimin , which is expressed on the bacterial cell surface 593 . Clustering of Tir molecules and then their interaction with intimin results in the tight attachment of the bacteria to the host cell surface 593 . Recruitment of the host Arp2 / 3 - mediated actin polymerization machinery occurs following an assortment of phosphorylation events on Tir 108 – 110 , 598 . The major determinant of actin - rich pedestal formation is the phosphorylation of tyrosine residue 474 by host tyrosine kinases such as Abl and c - Fyn 110 , 599 . This modified residue serves as a scaffold for the recruitment of another host protein , nck 110 . Nck recruitment ultimately recruits the host NPF , N - WASp , which in turn recruits and activates the Arp2 / 3 complex beneath the region of EPEC attachment 109 . The activation of the Arp2 / 3 complex generates the high branched network 35 of F - actin that ultimately induces pedestal formation . Other crucial host cell factors that promote proper pedestal formation include the Arp2 / 3 activating protein cortactin , as well as the F - actin bundling proteins calponin 1 , calponin 2 and SM22 536 , 600 , 601 . Recent findings also point towards a key role for the actin nucleator , mDia , in generating a source of short actin oligomers ( or seeds ) for the Arp2 / 3 complex during pedestal biogenesis 602 . Pedestal formation is further complicated by the discovery of a non - canonical role of host clathrin endocytic machinery components such as clathrin , dynamin 2 , CD2AP , epsin 1 , Eps15 and Hsc70 at the structures 338 , 568 ( p70 ) , 603 ( p15 ) . Interestingly , other host cytoskeletal elements such as intermediate filament proteins and spectrin proteins are also hijacked during pedestal generation and likely impart additional stability to the structures 537 . 1 . 9 . 2 . Salmonella enterica serovar Typhimurium S . Typhimurium cause their entry into the host cell by co - opting the Arp2 / 3 - mediated actin polymerization machinery 604 – 607 . Attachment of the bacteria to the host cell surface , followed immediately by the T3SS - mediated injection of an array of bacterial effectors into the host cytosol culminates in the formation of actin - rich membrane ruffles at the site of bacteria - host contact ( Figure 1 . 16 ) 604 , 605 , 607 . Ultimately , the actin - rich membrane ruffles engulf the attached bacteria into the host cytosol 604 , 605 , 607 . The bacterial effectors SopB , SopE , and SopE2 are the major determining factors for successful entry of S . Typhimurium into the host cell , as bacterial strains with all three effectors deleted fail to generate membrane ruffles , and consequently , are non - invasive 608 . Functionally , SopB is a lipid phosphatase and increases plasma membrane expression of phosphatidylinositol - 3 - phosphate ( PI3P ) , PIP2 and PIP3 604 , 607 . SopE and SopE2 activate the Rho family GTPases Cdc42 and Rac1 609 – 611 . The generation of phosphoinositides as well as active Cdc42 and Rac1 at the bacteria - host contact site results in the recruitment of the WAVE regulatory complex ( a cellular NPF ) , which in turn , activates the Arp2 / 3 complex 604 , 607 . Arp2 / 3 ultimately drives the formation of actin filaments against the plasma membrane forming the characteristic membrane ruffle 604 , 605 , 607 . Interestingly , the formin protein , FHOD1 , has also been demonstrated to control membrane ruffle formation via SopB 612 . SopB - mediated production of phosphoinositides results in the recruitment and activation of the Rho GTPase , RhoA 607 , 613 . RhoA activation of the host kinase ROCK , in turn , leads to FHOD recruitment to the bacteria - host contact site 612 . FHOD likely generates a small actin platform for the Arp2 / 3 complex to bind to and 36 extend into a branched F - actin network 612 . Remarkably , however , bacterial invasion is not completely abolished in the absence of Arp2 / 3 613 . Hanisch and colleagues demonstrate that , via SopB , myosin II - mediated contractility induces efficient bacterial invasion 613 . Thus , myosin II represents an additional , Arp2 / 3 - independent , mode of bacterial entry . Interestingly , when cells are depleted of both Arp2 / 3 and myosin II , bacterial invasion is completely eliminated 613 . The bacterial effector SipA is another T3SS injected factor which augments bacterial entry 614 – 616 . In the host cell , SipA stabilizes actin filaments during membrane ruffle formation and prevents their disassembly by host factors such as ADF / cofilin 614 – 616 . However , S . Typhimurium SipA mutants display only a marginal reduction in internalization levels 614 . 1 . 9 . 3 . Shigella flexneri Invasion S . flexneri is an invasive pathogen that also relies on actin - rich plasma membrane ruffling for their entry into cells ( Figure 1 . 17 ) 617 , 618 . These bacteria inject an array of T3SS effectors which manipulate actin cytoskeletal rearrangements beneath the plasma membrane 619 – 624 . The injected effectors IpaB and IpaC form a pore within the host plasma membrane to allow efficient movement of bacterial effectors into the host cell cytosol 625 . IpaC also activates the Arp2 / 3 complex via Src kinase and the NPF , cortactin 626 , 627 . The injected effector IpgB1 augments membrane ruffle formation through its ability to activate Rac1 , whose downstream targets further activate Arp2 / 3 628 . Another injected effector , IpgD , also promotes membrane ruffling through an as of yet unclear mechanism that involves PIP2 hydrolysis 629 . Two other effectors , IpgB2 and IpaA , are also implicated during the bacterial invasion process through activation of the GTPase Rho 630 – 633 . Following invasion , rapid vacuolar lysis releases the bacteria into the host cytosol . Actin - based motility Like L . monocytogenes , S . flexneri uses Arp2 / 3 - mediated actin polymerization at their cell surface to generate a motile comet / rocket tail ( Figure 1 . 18 ) 106 , 107 , 634 . Movement of the bacteria towards the host cell surface results in the deformation of the plasma membrane around the actin tail into a membranous protrusion 106 , 635 , 636 . As seen with L . 37 monocytogenes , projection of the membrane protrusion facilitates the cell - to - cell movement of S . flexneri bacteria into neighbouring cells 637 . The major determinant for comet / rocket tail formation is the bacterial surface protein IcsA 634 , 638 . Unlike the L . monocytogenes effector ActA , IcsA is not a functional mimic of cellular NPFs , and thus S . flexneri motility requires the activity of the Arp2 / 3 complex activator , N - WASp 634 , 638 – 640 . Rather , IcsA functionally mimics the Rho family GTPase Cdc42 , and upon its interaction with N - WASp at the bacterial surface , releases N - WASp from its autoinhibitory state 634 . N - WASp activation also relies on its phosphorylation by host tyrosine kinases such as Abl and Btk 641 , 642 . Additionally , recruitment of the host protein TOCA - 1 by another bacterial effector , VirB , is essential for activating N - WASp 643 . Eventually , recruitment and activation of the Arp2 / 3 complex results in the generation of a branched actin - containing comet / rocket tail at one pole of the bacteria 106 , 634 . Several host proteins have been identified as crucial factors for membrane protrusion formation and engulfment by neighboring cells . The formin , Dia1 , localizes to the actin core of membrane protrusions 644 . In cells depleted of Dia1 , cell - to - cell spreading of the bacteria is significantly perturbed ; however , the precise role of Dia1 within the membrane protrusion remains to be understood 644 . Myosin X is another component of the S . flexneri membrane protrusion 645 . Functionally , myosin X likely stabilizes the structures , as in cells inhibited for myosin X , shorter and thicker membrane protrusions are observed 645 . Myosin X most likely links the actin of the comet / rocket tail to the host plasma membrane 645 . Effective cell - to - cell spreading also relies on the clathrin endocytic machinery ; Fukumatsu and colleagues’ demonstrated clathrin and epsin - 1 localization to the membrane invaginations induced during membrane protrusion engulfment 349 . 1 . 10 . Rationale and research hypotheses L . monocytogenes exploit the host actin cytoskeleton during their cellular invasion , intracellular motility and cell - to - cell movement . Importantly , in order to propagate disease , the bacteria must generate motile actin - rich comet / rocket tails and membranous protrusions to propel the bacteria within and amongst host cells respectively . Although the minimal host components necessary for comet / rocket tail formation have been known for ~ 20 years , many more host components at the structures likely remain uncharacterized . In comparison , the mechanism behind L . monocytogenes membrane protrusion formation 38 remains poorly understood . The Enterobacteriaceae actin - hijacking bacteria EPEC , S . Typhimurium and S . flexneri routinely commandeer many of the same host proteins as L . monocytogenes during their infectious cycle . Like L . monocytogenes , the precise mechanisms regulating the formation of their actin - rich structures is not yet clear . Support for this comes from a recent mass - spectrometry screen of EPEC pedestals conducted in our lab that uncovered many host proteins not yet characterized during bacterial infections 646 . From this screen , I selected two proteins , palladin and cyclophilin A to examine during infections by actin - hijacking bacteria . Because actin - hijacking pathogens often utilize the same host proteins during their infections , I hypothesize that palladin and cyclophilin A are important host factors for overall infection , as well as for the formation of bacterially - derived actin - rich structures generated by actin - hijacking pathogens . L . monocytogenes generate large actin - rich membrane protrusions in order to spread from one cell to another . One of the longstanding questions regarding the cell - to - cell spreading process of L . monocytogenes is whether or not engulfment of the membrane protrusion occurs passively or actively by the host receiving cell . Importantly , several microbial pathogens have been demonstrated to exploit host endocytic pathways such clathrin - or caveolin - mediated endocytosis during their cellular invasion or cell - to - cell spreading 338 – 340 , 342 – 345 , 347 – 349 , 647 – 652 . Because of this , I hypothesize that the cell - to - cell spreading process of L . monocytogenes , and more specifically , the host cell engulfment of L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions , represents a large scale endocytic event . 39 1 . 11 . Contact of the motile bacteria with the host plasma membrane results in the formation of a finger - like membranous protrusion that projects the bacteria directly into neighboring host cells . Image reprinted with permission from the American Society for Microbiology Journals : Clinical Microbiology Reviews 21 , 591 . 58 Chapter 2 . Palladin compensates for the Arp2 / 3 complex and supports actin structures during Listeria infections The contents of this chapter are published . Dhanda , A . S . , Vogl , A . W . , Albraiki , S . E . , Otey , C . A . , Beck , M . R . , and Guttman J . A . ( 2018 ) . Palladin Compensates for the Arp2 / 3 Complex and Supports Actin Structures during Listeria Infections . mBio 9 ( 2 ) . pii : e02259 - 17 . doi : 10 . 1128 / mBio . 02259 - 17 . A . S . D . and J . A . G . conceived the study . A . W . V . performed electron microscopy imaging . S . E . A . purified L . monocytogenes ActA and palladin ( full - length , palladin - Ig3 , and palladinFPAA ) proteins and ran in vitro pyrene - actin polymerization assays . M . R . B generated GFP - palladinFPAA and provided additional palladin reagents as well as expertise . A . S . D performed all other experiments . C . A . O . provided reagents and palladin expertise . All authors analyzed the data and wrote the manuscript . 59 2 . 1 . Abstract Palladin is an important component of motile actin - rich structures and nucleates branched actin filament arrays in vitro . Here we examine the role of palladin during Listeria monocytogenes infections in order to tease out novel functions of palladin . We show that palladin is co - opted by L . monocytogenes during its cellular entry and intracellular motility . Depletion of palladin resulted in shorter and misshapen comet tails , and when actin - or VASP - binding mutants of palladin were overexpressed in cells , comet tails disintegrated or became thinner . Comet tail thinning resulted in parallel actin bundles within the structures . To determine whether palladin could compensate for the Arp2 / 3 complex , we overexpressed palladin in cells treated with the Arp2 / 3 inhibitor CK - 666 . In treated cells , bacterial motility could be initiated and maintained when levels of palladin were increased . To confirm these findings , we utilized a cell line depleted of multiple Arp2 / 3 complex subunits . Within these cells , L . monocytogenes failed to generate comet tails . When palladin was overexpressed in this Arp2 / 3 functionally null cell line , the ability of L . monocytogenes to generate comet tails was restored . Using purified protein components , we demonstrate that L . monocytogenes actin clouds and comet tails can be generated ( in a cell - free system ) by palladin in the absence of the Arp2 / 3 complex . Collectively , our results demonstrate that palladin can functionally replace the Arp2 / 3 complex during bacterial actin - based motility . 2 . 2 . Introduction The infectious cycle of the invasive and motile bacterium Listeria monocytogenes relies heavily on its ability to exploit the epithelial cell actin cytoskeleton . These bacteria require actin filaments for their uptake into epithelial cells 496 and for their formation of motile actin - rich structures generated within their host cells called comet tails 67 , 493 . During comet tail formation , L . monocytogenes recruit and activate the Arp2 / 3 complex to one of their poles through the N - WASP - mimicking bacterial protein , ActA 105 . This recruitment stimulates the force - generating , branched actin polymerization that is needed to propel L . monocytogenes within and amongst host cells , and functions at the molecular level similarly to lamellipodia in migrating eukaryotic cells 479 . 60 The actin - binding protein , palladin , is widely expressed in developing and adult vertebrate cells and tissues 201 , 202 , 655 . This multifunctional protein acts as a scaffolding protein by recruiting other actin - related proteins such as profilin 656 , VASP 205 , α - actinin 207 , ezrin 202 , PDLIM1 208 , Eps8 204 and LASP - 1 655 , to actin - rich structures within the cell . Palladin can directly crosslink actin filaments , an activity that has been linked to its Ig3 domain 186 , and can generate crosslinked actin filaments when pure preparations of palladin and monomeric actin are co - incubated in vitro 206 . In this study we explore the involvement of palladin during L . monocytogenes infections and simultaneously use L . monocytogenes infections as a model to study the functional roles of palladin . 2 . 3 . Results 2 . 3 . 1 . Palladin Localizes to L . monocytogenes Entry Sites and Actin - Rich Comet Tails , but not Listeriopods L . monocytogenes exploits the actin polymerization machinery at four distinct times : 1 ) for entry into cells , 2 ) as a cloud of F - actin surrounds immotile bacteria , 3 ) for intracellular motility and 4 ) for cell - to - cell spreading . When these microbes hijack the actin cytoskeleton they re - arrange it into dynamic morphological structures ( actin clouds , comet tails and listeriopods ) . To determine if palladin was recruited to these structures we infected HeLa cells with wild type L . monocytogenes and stained fixed cells for endogenous palladin . We found that palladin was recruited to bacterial entry sites , actin clouds and comet tails , but was absent from listeriopods ( Figure 2 . 1A ) . The altered localization of palladin in infected cells did not change its level of expression ( Figure 2 . 5 ) . Because these bacterially induced actin - based structures are highly dynamic , we sought to determine the recruitment characteristics of palladin in relation to actin . To do this we co - transfected Ptk2 cells with GFP - palladin and mKate - LifeAct and saw their simultaneous recruitment to actin clouds surrounding stationary bacteria as well as at motile comet tails ( Movie 2 . 1 ) . When comet tails pushed motile bacteria into the plasma membrane to initiate listeriopod formation , overall palladin intensity decreased to general cytoplasmic levels except at regions close to the bacteria - actin interface that continued to show increased palladin recruitment ( Movie 2 . 2 ) . 61 2 . 3 . 2 . Palladin Is Required for the Proper Formation and Motility of Comet Tails To investigate the importance of palladin during comet tail formation , we depleted palladin in HeLa cells using siRNA and then infected the cells with L . monocytogenes ( Figures 2 . 1B and 2 . 1E ) . We found no significant effects on bacterial invasion in cells with undetectable levels of palladin compared to control siRNA treated cells ( Fig 2 . 6A ) . Because bacteria could still invade host cells , we examined the morphology of comet tails in palladin - depleted cells and discovered that comet tails were significantly shorter in length compared to those in control siRNA treated cells ( Figure 2 . 1C ) . Actin staining also showed that in palladin - depleted cells , comet tails were distorted compared to their straighter counterparts in control cells ( Figures 2 . 1E - F ) . We quantified this difference by measuring the ratio of the full comet tail length to the shortest distance between the bacteria - tail interface and end of the comet tail ( tortuosity index ) and confirmed that comet tails in palladin - depleted cells were severely tortuous ( Figure 2 . 1D ) , further supporting its role within the eukaryotic cytoskeleton as an important actin - crosslinking protein . Interestingly , listeriopods appeared unaltered in the absence of palladin ( Fig S2 . 6B ) . 2 . 3 . 3 . Palladin Mutants Dramatically Alter L . monocytogenes Motility and F - actin Organization within Comet Tails The actin and VASP binding domains of palladin are important for its normal functioning 187 , 209 . We examined the influence of those regions on L . monocytogenes infections by overexpressing domain mutants of palladin that acted in dominant negative fashions ( Figure 2 . 2A ) . The actin binding ability of palladin has been tied to three key lysine residues ( K15 , K18 and K51 ) within its C - terminally located Ig3 domain ( Figure 2 . 2A ) . When a palladin variant mutated at these residues ( palladinK15 / 18 / 51A ) is expressed in cells , abnormal nuclear localization of palladin and extensive cytoskeletal perturbations in cultured epithelial cells are evident 187 . We co - transfected GFP - palladinK15 / 18 / 51A ( actin - binding mutant ) together with mKate - LifeAct into HeLa cells and viewed , via time – lapse imaging , motile bacteria during L . monocytogenes infections . We used the known nuclear localization of GFP - palladinK15 / 18 / 51A as a readout of cells that had functionally perturbed palladin and found that motile comet tails disintegrated at their distal ends , leaving behind a trail of 62 comet tail debris ( Figure 2 . 2B and Movie 2 . 3 ) . The crumbling comet tails moved at rates approximately two - fold slower than comet tails in cells overexpressing GFP - tagged wild - type palladin ( Figure 2 . 2C ) . The actin - associated protein VASP classically localizes to the surface of L . monocytogenes through direct interactions with the bacterial protein ActA ; however , it is also present throughout the entire comet tail ( Figure 2 . 2D ) . To assess the requirement of ActA expression on palladin recruitment to the bacterial surface , we utilized bacteria deleted in actA . Not surprisingly , palladin was unable to be redistributed to the surface of these mutant bacteria ( Figure 2 . 7 ) . Due to the importance of VASP during L . monocytogenes motility 219 , 221 , 657 , 658 and its association with palladin at actin - rich structures within the cell 209 , we examined the functional role of palladin - VASP interactions during L . monocytogenes infections by using a GFP - tagged palladin construct mutated in its VASP - binding polyproline motif ( GFP - palladinFPAA ) . We found dramatic alterations to the actin cytoskeleton in GFP - palladinFPAA expressing cells . In these cells , abnormal cytoplasmic clumps and bar - like structures were generated that were enriched with actin and VASP ( Figures 2 . 8A - B ) . We could not identify these unusual structures in either GFP - palladin or GFP - palladinK15 / 18 / 51A expressing cells ( Figure 2 . 8A ) . We used these abnormal actin - rich formations together with GFP as convenient markers for cells that were successfully transfected with GFP - palladinFPAA . When actin clouds were examined during live infections , the filamentous actin appeared notably diffuse around non - motile bacteria ( Figure 2 . 2B and Movie 2 . 4 ) . Strikingly , when comet tails were viewed , they became progressively thinner as they moved ( Figure 2 . 2B and Movie 2 . 4 ) . The thin comet tails also remained tethered to remnants of diffuse actin clouds that had stayed behind in their original location surrounding the L . monocytogenes bacteria prior to their launch into dynamic motility ( Figure 2 . 2B and Movie 2 . 4 ) . We also found that endogenous VASP was redistributed away from comet tails in GFP - palladinFPAA expressing cells ; however , its recruitment to the surface of bacteria remained unaltered ( Figure 2 . 2D ) . Motility rates of bacteria in GFP - palladinFPAA expressing cells decreased by 4 - fold as compared to GFP - palladin overexpressing cells ( Figure 2 . 2C ) . To gain further insight into the thinning events occurring at comet tails we used transmission electron microscopy . Comet tails normally exploit the Arp2 / 3 complex to generate a branched actin filament network . We found that the arrangement of F - actin throughout the thinned GFP - palladinFPAA comet tails contained parallel arrays of F - actin 63 whereas mock and GFP - palladin transfected cells did not ( Figures 2 . 2E - G′′ ) . Collectively , these findings show that the actin - binding and scaffolding roles of palladin are crucial for the proper formation and organization of branched actin filament arrays within comet tails . 2 . 3 . 4 . Palladin Compensates for the Arp2 / 3 Complex during L . monocytogenes Actin - Based Motility We have recently shown that palladin can generate actin filaments in vitro 206 . Based on these findings we investigated whether palladin’s apparent actin - nucleating ability could be exploited by L . monocytogenes to maintain its motility if the Arp2 / 3 complex was functionally defective . To do this we examined the motility of L . monocytogenes in cells overexpressing GFP - palladin , GFP - palladinK15 / 18 / 51A or GFP - palladinFPAA prior to ( and following ) perfusion of the Arp2 / 3 complex inhibitor , CK - 666 494 . A cessation of L . monocytogenes motility has already been demonstrated in infected cells treated with CK - 666 494 . We confirmed this by live - cell imaging L . monocytogenes infections of cells with endogenous levels of palladin and noticed an immediate disassembly of actin clouds and comet tails resulting in immotile bacteria when CK - 666 was introduced ( Figure 2 . 3A and Movie 2 . 5 ) . Remarkably , when GFP - palladin was overexpressed in cells , L . monocytogenes comet tails remained motile throughout treatment with CK - 666 ( Figure 2 . 3A and Movie 2 . 6 ) . Additionally , bacteria with actin clouds that were stationary prior to the addition of CK - 666 in GFP - palladin overexpressing cells were still able to generate comet tails and became motile in a manner indistinguishable from bacteria in untreated cells suggesting that exogenous palladin is not functioning solely as a stabilizer of pre - existing comet tails during treatment with CK - 666 ( Movie 2 . 7 ) . Bacterial motility was also evident in cells overexpressing GFP - palladinK15 / 18 / 51A or GFP - palladinFPAA ( actin - or VASP - binding palladin mutants ) after CK - 666 was introduced ( Figure 2 . 3A and Movies 2 . 8 and 2 . 9 ) albeit with the crumbling and thinning comet tail phenotypes described earlier . To gain further insight into this novel function of palladin , we tracked the speed of motile bacteria by time - lapse microscopy ( Figure 2 . 3B ) . Before the addition of CK - 666 , motile L . monocytogenes in cells with endogenous amounts of palladin moved at an average speed of 8 . 990 µm / min ( Figure 2 . 3C ) . Following CK - 666 treatment , bacterial speeds dropped significantly to an average of 0 . 279 µm / min ( Figure 2 . 3C ) . Although the majority of motile bacteria came to a complete stop after the introduction of CK - 666 , a fraction of the bacteria displayed a slow ( 1 . 281 µm / min ) , jerky - type of movement ( Figure 2 . 3B ) . Interestingly , L . 64 monocytogenes motility rates in CK - 666 treated cells overexpressing GFP - tagged wild type palladin were unaltered upon treatment with CK - 666 and displayed speeds similar to those of bacteria in wild type cells prior to the drug treatment ( Figure 2 . 3B - C ) . To further characterize this novel function of palladin , we set out to examine bacterial actin - based motility in cells depleted of the Arp2 / 3 complex . To do this , we utilized a recently established Arpc2 conditional knockout cell line 659 . In these cells , loss of the Arpc2 gene product ( p34 ) also caused the depletion of additional Arp2 / 3 complex subunits including Arp2 and Arp3 659 . A challenge in studying L . monocytogenes infections in Arpc2 - / - cells was that the bacteria could not invade the cells . To overcome this we pre - infected wild type cells with L . monocytogenes and then mixed the infected wild type cells with Arpc2 - / - cells expressing GFP - palladin or the GFP empty vector and allowed the infection to proceed for 16 hours ; ultimately resulting in the cell - to - cell spread of bacteria into Arpc2 - / - cells . As expected , bacteria within Arpc2 - / - cells expressing GFP alone were unable to generate F - actin at their surface and formed intracellular clusters ( Figure 2 . 4A ) . However , when Arpc2 - / - cells overexpressed GFP - palladin , L . monocytogenes generated actin - rich comet tails enriched with palladin ( Figure 2 . 4A ) , as was the case with wild type cells expressing GFP - palladin ( Figure 2 . 4A ) . To definitively establish that palladin can induce F - actin nucleation around bacteria as well as promote the formation and elongation of actin - rich comet tails in the absence of the Arp2 / 3 complex , we modified a previously developed cell free protein reconstitution assay 107 . This assay allows for the generation of actin clouds and comet tails in a cell free system when the bacteria are mixed together with purified components of the actin polymerization machinery that include the Arp2 / 3 complex , profilin , cofilin , gelsolin and F - actin . As expected , we were able to generate actin clouds and comet tails when the protein constituents contained all of the aforementioned components ( Figure 2 . 4B ) . To test if purified palladin could functionally replace the Arp2 / 3 complex , we substituted palladin for the Arp2 / 3 complex . We found that full - length palladin was capable of nucleating F - actin clouds around L . monocytogenes and could polymerize comet tails behind the bacteria ( Figure 2 . 4B ) . We also identified long thin palladin - generated comet tails tethered to clumps of actin ( Figure 2 . 9 ) . None of these structures were generated when the actin - binding domain of palladin ( Ig3 - palladin ) was used in place of full - length palladin ( Figure 2 . 4B ) . When a palladin variant mutated in its VASP - binding region ( palladinFPAA ) was used in place of the wild type full - length form , actin clouds and comet tails associated with 65 the bacteria failed to form ( Figure 2 . 10 ) . However , this mutant form of palladin did produce two populations of F - actin arrays , linear F - actin bundles and disorganized F - actin clumps ( Figure 2 . 10 ) that were reminiscent of the structures generated in cells overexpressing palladinFPAA ( Figure 2 . 2B ) . L . monocytogenes ActA augments the polymerization activity of the Arp2 / 3 complex 105 . Similarly , in vitro actin polymerization rates of reactions containing both Arp2 / 3 and ActA are enhanced when compared to reactions using Arp2 / 3 alone 105 . Using pyrene - actin polymerization assays we found that ActA also enhanced palladin’s ability to nucleate and polymerize actin ( Figure 2 . 4C ) . 2 . 4 . Discussion In summary , we have described several novel ways that palladin influences actin - rich structures generated during L . monocytogenes infections . When palladin is depleted from cells , comet tails have a tortuous morphology and a diminished length . When specific amino acids are altered , comet tails crumble and actin organization switches from branched networks to parallel arrays . Moreover , we show that palladin can functionally replace the Arp2 / 3 complex in infected cells as well as in a cell free system by promoting the actin - based motility of the bacteria . How does this protein mechanistically accomplish this ? The mutation of three lysine amino acids ( K15 / 18 / 51A ) in the Ig3 domain of palladin that causes crumbling comet tails has previously been shown to severely influence the crosslinking function of the protein , diminishing it to background levels 187 . Biochemical evidence has demonstrated that when bound to actin , palladin can also dimerize , which facilitates its crosslinking activity 188 . Thus , we postulate that crumbling comet tails may arise due to the diminished ability of palladin to bind actin . In turn , this would lower palladin’s ability to dimerize and thus crosslink actin filaments within the comet tail dendritic meshwork despite the known presence of other potent actin - crosslinkers such as α - actinin and fascin at the comet tails 114 , 578 . Although palladin is crucial for proper comet tail formation , whether its activity is also important during listeriopod formation will require further study . We show that palladin is shed from the actin of the listeriopods , suggesting that it likely has no role in bacterial cell - 66 to - cell spreading events . The altered distribution of actin - associated proteins that are present in comet tails , but are eliminated from listeriopods has also been reported for  - actinin 115 . Interestingly other proteins work in the reverse manner ; being recruited to listeriopods , but not comet tails 115 , 534 . The differences in actin - associated components are likely due to the morphological organization of the actin filaments within the structures as comet tails contain branched actin arrays and despite Arp2 / 3 being present at the bacterial actin interface within listeriopods , the majority of actin within those protrusions are organized in a parallel arrangement through formins 115 , 534 , 539 . The role of VASP during L . monocytogenes infections has been studied extensively at the bacterial surface where it directly binds to ActA and regulates L . monocytogenes motility rates 219 , 660 . However , VASP also localizes within the comet tail and here we show that an absence of VASP from comet tails in palladinFPAA - expressing cells dramatically influences the organization of actin filaments , changing them from branched arrays to parallel . In addition to the altered organization of F - actin within the comet tails , this mutant form of palladin also dramatically alters the cytoskeleton of the host cell itself as it generates actin - rich cytoplasmic clumps within the cell . Similar clumps were also generated in the cell - free reconstitution assays when palladinFPAA was used in place of wild - type palladin suggesting that either the lack of the VASP binding domain itself ( together with actin ) or unknown interactions of the other components in the assays with this palladin mutant are responsible for the observed clumping phenotype . Others have found that the absence of VASP from actin - rich structures increases F - actin branching 216 , which may be influencing the observed actin clumps . This would be counterintuitive to our observation of ‘parallel’ structures within the palladin FPAA comet tails . However , in those comet tails VASP remains at the bacterial surface while absent from the length of the comet tail . At the bacterial surface VASP could function by regulating the elongation of the actin filaments by binding to barbed filament ends associated with the bacterial surface in a process dependent on binding palladin . Our most significant discovery was the demonstration that palladin can functionally replace the Arp2 / 3 complex likely through its ability to nucleate and polymerize F - actin into actin clouds and motile comet tails . We also showed that ActA further enhanced palladin’s actin nucleating activity , but to a much lesser extent than that generated by the Arp2 / 3 complex . The substantial disparity between Arp2 / 3 and palladin + ActA nucleation / polymerization activities suggests that another mechanism could be involved 67 during the generation of palladin - mediated actin comet tails . In addition to its known actin nucleating and crosslinking roles , palladin is efficient at stabilizing actin filaments 206 . Palladin also dimerizes upon actin binding 188 and this could further enhance both filament crosslinking and stabilization while also providing additional nucleation sites for actin . Thus , as an alternative strategy , palladin may use those properties to enhance its nucleating abilities at L . monocytogenes actin - rich structures . Because palladin and the Arp2 / 3 complex are abundant proteins in essentially all epithelial cells , it remains unclear to what extent the replacement of the Arp2 / 3 complex with palladin would actually occur during in vivo infections . Our evidence that palladin itself can nucleate and extend F - actin networks in the complete absence of the Arp2 / 3 complex is different from what has been shown previously with  - actinin and fascin as these proteins can only extend actin networks generated by the Arp2 / 3 complex but not nucleate them 114 . Because palladin levels are highly elevated at the motile leading edge of normal 205 and wounded cells 661 – 663 , as well as the fact that palladin is highly upregulated in motile cancer cells 664 – 667 , we propose a bona fide cellular function for the actin nucleation role of palladin in enhancing actin - based motility events within the cell . Overall , these findings could have broad implications for an array of cell biology 661 , 668 , tumor biology 203 , 664 – 667 and microbial pathogenesis 540 fields . 2 . 5 . Materials and Methods 2 . 5 . 1 . Cell Culture Human cervical ( HeLa ) and Potorous tridactylus kidney ( Ptk2 ) epithelial cells were obtained from American Type Culture Collection ( ATCC ) ( numbers CCL - 2 and CCL - 56 respectively ) . HeLa cells were cultured in Dulbecco’s modified Eagle’s medium ( DMEM ) containing high glucose ( Hyclone , GE Healthcare ) and were supplemented with 10 % fetal bovine serum ( FBS ) ( Gibco , Thermo Fisher Scientific ) . Ptk2 cells were cultured in DMEM / F - 12 ( 1 : 1 ) ( Hyclone , GE Healthcare ) supplemented with 10 % FBS . Both cell lines were maintained in a cell culture incubator ( 37 °C , 5 % CO2 ) . To obtain Arpc2 - / - cells , the parental mouse embryonic fibroblast ( MEF ) cell line designated 10 - 4 was treated with puromycin dihydrochloride ( Sigma ) and 4 - hydroxy - tamoxifen ( 4 - OHT , Sigma ) as described previously 659 . To seed cells for experiments , flasks or culture dishes with cells were washed 3X with Dulbecco’s phosphate buffered saline without Ca2 + and Mg2 + ( PBS 68 [ - / - ] ) ( Gibco , Thermo Fisher Scientific ) , trypsinized with 0 . 05 % Trypsin - EDTA ( Gibco , Thermo Fisher Scientific ) and seeded onto clear polystyrene 6 - well plates ( Corning ) containing glass coverslips . For electron microscopy experiments , flexible silicone elastomer membranes ( Flexcell International ) were used in place of glass coverslips . 2 . 5 . 2 . Bacterial Strains and Growth Conditions The bacterial strains used were L . monocytogenes strains EGD BUG 600 and Δ actA ( Gifted by Dr . Pascale Cossart ) . All L . monocytogenes strains were grown at 37 °C using either brain heart infusion ( BHI ) agar or broth ( BD Biosciences ) . 2 . 5 . 3 . Listeria monocytogenes Infections To infect cultured cells , overnight shaken broth cultures of L . monocytogenes were diluted 10X in BHI broth and then incubated at 37 °C in a shaking incubator until A600 = 1 . 00 . Once cultures reached A600 = 1 . 00 , bacteria were spun down for 5 minutes at 10 , 000 rpm ( 25 °C ) and washed with PBS [ - / - ] . Pelleted bacteria were re - suspended with serum - free media then diluted 100X . Diluted bacteria were added onto culture plates containing host cells and incubated for 30 minutes to study bacterial internalization or at least 6 hours to study comet tails and listeriopod formation . To infect Arpc2 - / - cells , wild type cells were infected for 2 hours , collected from culture plates and overlaid onto culture plates containing uninfected Arpc2 - / - cells where the infection was allowed to proceed for an additional 14 - 18 hours . 2 . 5 . 4 . Antibodies and Reagents Antibodies and reagents used in this study included : Alexa Fluor 594 - , 488 - and 350 - conjugated phalloidin ( Invitrogen ) ; Alexa Fluor 594 - , 488 - , and 350 - conjugated goat anti - rabbit and goat anti - mouse antibodies ( 2 µg / mL , Invitrogen ) ; mouse anti - palladin ( 50 µg / mL for immunofluorescence and 500 µg / mL for Western blot , Novus Biologicals ) ; rabbit anti - palladin ( 0 . 002 µg / mL for immunofluorescence and 0 . 002 µg / mL for Western blotting , Proteintech Group ) ; rabbit anti - VASP ( 1 . 1 µg / mL for immunofluorescence and 0 . 1 µg / mL for Western blotting , Sigma ) ; rabbit anti - p34 ( 10 µg / mL for immunofluorescence , 69 Millipore ) ; rabbit anti - actin ( 0 . 1 µg / mL for Western blot , Abcam ) , rabbit anti - calnexin ( 1 : 2000 for Western blot , Sigma ) ; HRP - conjugated goat anti - rabbit and goat anti - mouse antibodies ( 1 µg / mL , Invitrogen ) ; purified profilin , cofilin , gelsolin , Arp2 / 3 complex , rhodamine - actin , skeletal actin and ATP ( Cytoskeleton Inc ) ; methylcellulose CP4000 ( Sigma ) ; DABCO ( Sigma ) ; DTT ( Sigma - Roche ) ; and CK - 666 ( 100 µM , Abcam ) . 2 . 5 . 5 . Immunolocalization For immunofluorescence studies , cells were fixed at room temperature for 15 minutes using pre - warmed ( 37 ºC ) 3 % paraformaldehyde ( prepared in 150 mM NaCl , 4 mM Na / K PO 4 , 5 . 0 mM KCl , pH 7 . 3 ) and then washed 3X with PBS [ - / - ] . Cells were permeabilized with room temperate 0 . 1 % Triton X - 100 ( prepared in PBS [ - / - ] ) for 5 minutes and then washed 3X with PBS [ - / - ] . Samples treated with mouse anti - palladin antibodies required permeabilization with −20 °C acetone for 10 minutes followed by air drying at room temperature for 30 minutes . All samples were then blocked with 5 % normal goat serum ( prepared in PBS [ - / - ] ) for 20 minutes after which samples were incubated overnight at 4 °C with primary antibodies prepared in TPBS / BSA ( PBS [ - / - ] , 0 . 5 % Tween - 20 , 0 . 1 % bovine serum albumin [ BSA ] ) . Following this , samples were washed 3X with TPBS / BSA for 10 minutes and then treated with secondary antibodies ( Alexa Fluor 594 - or 488 - conjugated goat anti - rabbit or goat anti - mouse ) at room temperature for 2 hours . To visualize F - actin , samples were incubated with Alexa Fluor 594 - , 488 - or 350 - conjugated phalloidin ( prepared in PBS [ - / - ] ) for 20 minutes . Samples were washed 3X with PBS [ - / - ] and mounted onto glass microscope slides using Prolong Diamond antifade mountant containing DAPI ( Invitrogen ) . 2 . 5 . 6 . Lysate Preparation and Western Blotting Lysates were prepared by washing the samples 3X with pre - warmed PBS [ - / - ] and then treating the samples with ice - chilled RIPA lysis buffer ( 150 mM NaCl , 50 mM Tris , pH 7 . 4 , 5 mM EDTA , 1 % Nonidet P - 40 , 1 % deoxycholic acid , 10 % SDS ) with cOmplete™ Mini EDTA - free protease inhibitor cocktail ( Roche ) on ice for 5 minutes . Cells were disrupted using cell scrapers and lysates collected into microcentrifuge tubes . Lysates were spun at 4 °C and 10 , 000 g for 10 minutes to pellet cellular debris ; supernatants were collected into fresh microcentrifuge tubes and immediately stored at −80 °C . Protein concentrations were determined using a bicinchoninic acid ( BCA ) assay kit ( Pierce ) . For 70 Western blotting , lysates samples were first prepared in 6X Laemmli buffer then boiled for 10 minutes . Equal amounts of protein were loaded onto 10 % SDS - polyacrylamide gels and subsequently resolved by electrophoresis . Following separation , gels were rinsed in water for 5 minutes and then transferred onto nitrocellulose membranes using a Trans - Blot® SD semi - dry transfer cell ( Bio - Rad ) . After the transfer , the membranes were washed for 5 minutes in TBST ( Tris - buffered saline , 0 . 05 % Tween - 20 ) , blocked with 4 % Blotto ( Santa Cruz Biotechnology ) prepared in TBST and then treated with primary antibodies ( diluted in TBST , 1 % BSA ) overnight at 4 °C . Membranes were washed 3X with TBST for 10 minutes each prior to incubating with secondary antibodies ( HRP - conjugated goat anti - rabbit or goat anti - mouse ) for 1 hour at room temperature . Membranes were treated with Western Lightning Plus - ECL ( PerkinElmer ) following the manufacturer’s instructions and visualized using a Fujifilm LAS - 4000 imager ( Fujifilm ) . To confirm equal loading , membranes were stripped of bound antibodies with mild stripping buffer ( 1 . 5 % glycine , 0 . 1 % SDS , 1 % Tween - 20 , pH 2 . 2 ) and re - probed using anti - actin or anti - calnexin targeting antibodies as outlined above . 2 . 5 . 7 . DNA Constructs All palladin constructs used consisted of the major 90 kDa isoform , commonly referred to as isoform # 4 . These included GFP vectors containing wildtype palladin , and the actin - binding mutant GFP - palladinK15 / 18 / 51A10 . GFP - palladinFPAA , the VASP - binding mutant construct , was generated from the phrGFPIIN - palladin ( human isoform # 4 ) construct . For vector controls , the phrGFPIIN vector ( Stratagene ) was utilized . The phenylalanine and proline residues found in the polyproline region of palladin were both mutated to alanine using site - directed mutagenesis with the following primers : 5’ - GTGCCCGACGTGGCCGCACTGCCGCCGCCACCA - 3’ and 5’ - TGGTGGCGGCGGCAGTGCGGCCACGTCGGGCAC - 3’ . Plasmids containing mKate - LifeAct or eGFP - LifeAct were a gift from Dr . Michael Davidson ( Addgene plasmid # 54697 and 54610 respectively ) . 2 . 5 . 8 . Microscopy and Live Cell Imaging Images were acquired using a Leica DMI4000B ( Leica Microsystems ) inverted fluorescent microscope fitted with a Hamamatsu Orca R2 CCD camera ( Hamamatsu Photonics ) . All devices were controlled by MetaMorph Imaging System software 71 ( Universal Imaging ) . Images obtained were evaluated using Metamorph Imaging System software or ImageJ . For live cell imaging , a Chamlide IC top stage incubator system was used to maintain a constant temperature and environment of 37 °C and 5 % humidified CO2 gas in air . Bacterial motility rates and comet tails were analyzed using ImageJ . For CK - 666 studies , DMEM ( without phenol red ) + 10 % FBS containing 100 µM CK - 666 ( prepared in DMSO ) was perfused into magnetic coverslip - containing chambers ( Chamlide ) during the infections at indicated times . 2 . 5 . 9 . Cell Culture Transfections All DNA transfections of cultured cells were performed using jetPEI or jetPRIME transfection reagents ( Polyplus Transfection ) and were carried out according to the manufacturer’s instructions . Briefly , cells were transfected and allowed to incubate at 37 °C for 4 hours . Following this , media was replaced and cells were incubated for 24 hours at 37 °C to allow the expression of the respective gene product . Transfected cells were either fixed for viewing by immunofluorescence microscopy or imaged live by time - lapse microscopy . 2 . 5 . 10 . Palladin RNAi Knockdown A smart pool ( ON - Targetplus siRNA ) of 4 palladin siRNA and 4 non - targeting control siRNA were purchased from Dharmacon ( GE Healthcare ) . Transfections were performed using the siRNA transfection reagent INTERFERin ( Polyplus transfection ) following the manufacturer’s instructions . Briefly , 0 . 1 mL of serum - free media containing 50 nM siRNA duplexes and INTERFERin was added to cells contained in clear polystyrene 24 well culture plates . To obtain cells with undetectable levels of palladin protein , cells required a 72 hour incubation period following the siRNA treatment . 2 . 5 . 11 . Electron Microscopy Media was replaced with fixative ( 1 . 5 % paraformaldehyde , 1 . 5 % glutaraldehyde , 0 . 1 M sodium cacodylate , pH7 . 3 , rt ) , left for 2 - 3 hours , and then the fixative was replaced with buffer ( 0 . 1M sodium cacodylate , pH7 . 3 , rt ) . The membranes , with attached cells , were gently cut away from cell culture dishes and then further cut into 1 - 2 cm2 pieces . The pieces were placed in glass vials and then washed twice ( 10 minutes each wash ) with 72 fresh buffer . The samples were post - fixed for 1 hour on ice with 1 % osmium tetroxide in 0 . 1M sodium cacodylate ( pH 7 . 3 ) . The samples were washed three times ( 10 minutes each wash ) with ddH2O ( rt ) and then stained en bloc with 1 % aqueous uranyl acetate ( rt ) . The membranes were again washed three times with ddH2O ( rt ) and then dehydrated through an ascending series of ethyl alcohols ( 30 % , 50 % , 70 % , 95 % , 2X100 % - 10 minutes each ) followed by two treatments with propylene oxide ( 15 minutes each ) . The samples were then placed in 1 : 1 propylene oxide : EMBED 812 resin ( Electron microscopy Sciences , Hatfield , PA ) and left overnight . The following day , the membranes were passed through two changes of 100 % EMBED 812 resin and then placed on glass slides with the cells face - up . Embedding capsules were filled with resin , inverted onto the membranes , and then the slides with membranes and embedding capsules placed in an oven ( 60 °C ) for the resin to polymerize for 48 hours . After polymerization , the capsules ( with embedded cells ) were carefully separated from the membranes that remained attached to the slides . The cell layers at the surfaces of the block were sectioned en face using a Leica ultramicrotome and collected onto copper grids . The sections were stained with uranyl acetate and lead citrate , and then viewed and images collected using a FEI Tecnai G2 Spirit Electron Microscope operated at 120 kV . 2 . 5 . 12 . Protein purification Full - length 90 - kDa human palladin was subcloned into the pTBSG expression vector to allow for expression of a His6 fusion protein . The construct was transformed into BL21 ( DE3 ) E . coli cells ( NEB , Ipswich , MA ) and cells were grown at 37 °C until OD600 reached 0 . 6 in ZYM - 5052 auto - induction media . Cell cultures were pelleted down and resuspended in lysis buffer ( 20 mM sodium phosphate , 300 mM NaCl , 2 mM DTT , 10 % glycerol , pH 7 . 4 ) , followed by sonication and clearing of cell lysate by centrifugation . Supernatant was incubated with PROTEINDEXTM Ni - PentaTM agarose 6 Fast Flow ( Marvelgent Biosciences Inc . , Canton , MA ) slurry overnight at 4 °C before protein was purified according to manufacturer’s guidelines . The elution fraction was dialyzed into S - column buffer A ( 25 mM KH2PO4 , 50 mM NaCl , 2 mM DTT , pH 6 . 5 ) before loading onto cation - exchange column on an ÄKTA FPLC ( GE Healthcare ) with a HiPrepTM SP XL column . The protein was eluted using a gradient with a target of 100 % buffer B ( 25 mM KH2PO4 , 1 M NaCl , 2 mM DTT , pH 6 . 5 ) . Fractions containing palladin were confirmed by SDS - PAGE and protein was dialyzed into storage buffer ( 20 mM Hepes , 150 mM NaCl , 73 pH 7 . 5 , 2 mM TCEP ) . Purification of L . monocytogenes ActA - His ( strain DPL1545 ) was performed as previously described 105 . The Arp2 / 3 protein complex was purchased from ( Cytoskeleton , Inc . ) . Actin was purified from rabbit muscle acetone powder ( PelFreez Biologicals ) by using the method of 669 and gel - filtered on 16 / 60 Sephacryl S - 200 column ( GE Healthcare Life Sciences ) . Purified monomeric actin was stored at 4 °C in G - buffer ( 5 mM Tris , pH 8 , 0 . 1 mM CaCl2 , 0 . 2 mM DTT , 0 . 2 mM ATP and 0 . 02 % sodium azide ) and used within 2 – 4 weeks . Pyrene - labelled actin was prepared by the reaction of N - ( 1 - pyrenyl ) iodoacetamide ( Sigma - Aldrich ) with gel - filtered monomeric actin ( G - actin ) as described previously 670 . 2 . 5 . 13 . Reconstitution of Listeria actin clouds and comet tails using purified proteins On the day of the experiments , fresh stocks of the following were prepared : assay buffer ( 10 mM HEPES pH 7 . 5 , 0 . 1 M KCl , 1 mM MgCl 2 , 0 . 1 mM CaCl 2 , 1 mM ATP ) , ATP / DABCO / DTT ( ADD ) mix ( make by mixing together 20 µL of 30 mM ATP / 60 mM , 10 µL 2 . 2 mM DABCO , and 5 µL 0 . 2 M DTT ) , 1 % methylcellulose CP4000 , 10 % BSA and 48 µM Mg - F - actin . To reconstitute actin polymerization around L . monocytogenes ( BUG 600 ) the following reagents were added in order to a Eppendorf tube ( at the following final concentrations ) to create the reaction mix : BSA ( 0 . 5 % ) ; cofilin ( 3 . 7 µM ) ; profilin ( 2 . 5 µM ) ; gelsolin ( 50 nM ) ; one of Arp2 / 3 ( 75 nM ) or palladin ( full - length , Ig3 - palladin or palladinFPAA 4 . 875 µM ) ; ADD ( 3 . 0 µL per 24 µL reaction mix ) ; rhodamine - G - actin ( 1 µM ) ; L . monocytogenes in assay buffer ( 2x10 8 bacteria / mL ) ; Mg - F - actin ( 7 . 6 µM ) and methylcellulose ( 0 . 23 % ) . Anywhere from 2 to 5 µL of the reaction mix were spotted onto a 35 mm Fluorodish ( WPI Inc ) or standard glass microscope slide pre - marked with a dakocytomation pen and then covered with a 12 mm glass circle coverslip . Coverslips were added carefully so as to not squish down against the droplet . Samples were then placed onto the microscope to begin phase - contrast as well as fluorescent microscopy observation of actin cloud and comet tail formation . 2 . 5 . 14 . Pyrene fluorescence assay Pyrenyl actin and unlabeled G - actin were mixed together to make 5 μM , 5 % pyrene labeled G - actin stock . Labeled G - actin ( 100 μL ) was incubated with ( 10 μL ) of 10X priming solution ( 10 mM EGTA and 1 mM MgCl 2 ) for 2 min , then polymerization was induced by 74 adding 0 . 37 μM Arp 2 / 3 , 10μM full - length palladin with or without 0 . 3 μM ActA . All reactions were performed in G - buffer ( without KCl ) . Pyrene fluorescence was measured immediately with excitation at 365 nm and emission at 385 nm on a PTI fluorescence spectrometer . 2 . 5 . 15 . Statistical Analysis Statistical analysis was performed with Student’s unpaired t test ( Mann - Whitney U test for nonparametric tests ) or 1 - way ANOVA with the Tukey post - hoc test when comparing means of two or more groups in GraphPad Prism version 6 . 01 . All data are presented as bar graphs with mean ± SEM unless indicated otherwise . Experiments were performed at least 3 times ( n = 3 ) and the person who performed the experiment performed all of the enumeration and statistical analyses . All data involving immunofluorescence microscopy were obtained from experiments performed at least 3 times ( n = 3 ) . The presented microscopy images are representative of experiments performed . In Fig . 1C , at least 45 comet tails were measured per condition , per experiment ( 230 and 162 comet tails in total were measured in Ctrl and KD cells respectively ) . In Fig . 2 . 1D , at least 45 comet tails were measured per condition , per experiment ( 116 and 110 comet tails in total were measured in Ctrl and KD cells respectively ) . Data in Fig . 2 . 1C depicts average values ( ± standard deviation ) for 3 independent experiments ; 99 % confidence interval indicated by asterisk . Data in Fig . 2 . 1D depicts average values ( ± standard error ) for 3 independent experiments ; 99 % confidence interval indicated by asterisk . In Fig . 2 . 2C , data shows average values ( ± standard error ) of at least 10 rate measurements , which were performed per group over the course of 3 independent experiments ; 99 % confidence interval indicated by asterisks . For Fig . 2 . 3B , the instantaneous speed of 19 , 16 , 13 and 4 bacteria in cells expressing mKate - LifeAct , mKate - LifeAct and GFP - palladin , mKate - LifeAct and GFP - palladinK15 / 18 / 51A or mKate - LifeAct and GFP - palladinFPAA respectively was measured with the total time of bacteria being measured ranging from a minimum of approximately 5 minutes up to approximately 10 minutes . For Fig . 2 . 3C , data show average value ( ± standard error ) ; 90 % and 99 % confidence intervals indicated by asterisks . 75 2 . 6 . Figures 76 77 Figure 2 . 1 .
