General Discussion The commonly used model of the intracellular lifecycle of L . monocytogenes was first described 30 years ago by Tilney and Portnoy 493 . For the next ~ 20 years , many groups set their sights on uncovering the precise molecular mechanisms governing the initial invasion of the bacteria into host cells and actin comet / rocket tail formation 67 , 107 , 338 , 347 , 474 , 478 , 479 , 493 , 497 , 509 , 542 , 543 , 576 , 763 , 764 . Along the way , and through using the L . monocytogenes actin - generated structures as research tools , several fundamental discoveries to general eukaryotic cell biology were also realized , such as the functional characterization of the Arp2 / 3 complex 52 , 105 , 107 , 494 , profilin 107 , 765 , 766 and VASP 219 , 220 , 576 , as well as the identification of non - canonical functions for the clathrin - mediated endocytic machinery 347 , 348 . It wasn’t until Pust and colleagues ( 2005 ) pivotal investigation of ezrin during L . monocytogenes membrane protrusion formation and cell - to - cell spreading , that researchers began to seriously examine the host and bacterial factors involved during the bacterial dissemination process 249 . To date , only a handful of factors have been identified at the bacterial membrane protrusions 249 , 534 , 539 . Moreoever , prior to the work presented in this thesis , no host or bacterial components had been characterized at the invaginations generated in host cells that receive the L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions . Taken together , despite the several decades’ worth of research into L . monocytogenes infections , the mechanistic model of L . monocytogenes dissemination remains incomplete . To spread in tissues , L . monocytogenes bacteria must first become motile within the host intracellular environment . The minimal host constituents required to induce L . monocytogenes actin - based motility via comet / rocket tails have been known for many years 107 . However , like many of the actin - rich structures generated normally in eukaryotic cells , factors that are involved during L . monocytogenes comet / rocket tail formation continue to be discovered . This is clearly evident from the recent discoveries of stathmin , tubulin , transgelin , crmp1 , and lamellipodin at these structures over the past 5 years 195 , 217 – 219 . Research continues as these host proteins are essential for disease progression through their ability to avoid autophagy and induce membrane protrusion formation 249 , 534 , 539 , 583 , 584 . Conversely , the comet / rocket tails themselves have proved to be useful tools to help uncover new functions of previously known proteins . An example of this is the actin - associated protein , palladin , which was initially revealed to be present at actin - rich bacterial structures through a mass spectrometry screen of isolated EPEC pedestals 258 performed by our laboratory 646 . In the eukaryotic cell , palladin is a crucial component of several actin - rich structures such as lamellipodia , stress fibers , dorsal ruffles , podosomes and neural growth cones 201 , 204 , 205 , 209 , 661 , 769 . In addition to this , palladin directly interacts with actin filaments 186 , 187 , 206 . Given this , as well as the fact that the role of palladin during bacterial infections was unknown , it was an appropriate candidate to investigate during L . monocytogenes infections , and in particular , at comet / rocket tails . My research identified palladin at the actin - rich L . monocytogenes invasion sites , “clouds” surrounding immotile bacteria and comet / rocket tails . Shortly after this , our collaborator Moriah Beck demonstrated that palladin could form branched actin filament arrays when purified palladin and G - actin were co - incubated in vitro 206 . Interestingly , several studies also highlighted the ability of eukaryotic cells to undergo cellular motility even in the absence of the Arp2 / 3 complex 93 , 142 , 770 . With this in mind , we asked the question , could palladin generate branched actin filaments around L . monocytogenes and ultimately form into a comet / rocket tail in the absence of the Arp2 / 3 complex ? This is a crucial question in cell biology , since the Arp2 / 3 complex has long been considered as the driving force behind branched F - actin - mediated motility . To test this , we depleted cells of the Arp2 / 3 complex using the inhibitor CK - 666 . In cells inhibited for the Arp2 / 3 complex , comet / rocket tails disassembled . Amazingly , in Arp2 / 3 knockout cells which we overexpressed palladin , comet / rocket tails maintained their motility . In my continued examination of palladin , I found that it was absent from the actin - rich L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions which are used to propel the bacteria into neighbouring host cells . The phenomenon of protein exclusion at membrane protrusions also holds true for other actin crosslinkers , such as  - actinin 1 and nexilin 535 , 578 . Conversely , during my examination of CypA and CD147 , I discovered that these host proteins were present exclusively at L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions , but not actin clouds or comet / rocket tails . Consequently , an important question emerged from this ; why might the protein constituents of comet / rocket tails differ from those found at membrane protrusions and what is the functional consequence of this switch in protein components ? The L . monocytogenes comet / rocket tail consists of a dense dendritic - like network of F - actin within the structures 106 , 113 , 479 , 493 . However , comet / rocket tails are not exclusively formed from branched actin ; Jasnin and colleagues ( 2013 ) performed a cryo - electron microscopic examination of L . monocytogenes comet / rocket tails and found stiff 259 crosslinked bundles of actin filaments within the structures 113 . Brieher and colleagues ( 2004 ) also demonstrated long fascin - bundled F - actin , resembling a hollow cylinder , at the edges of the comet / rocket tail 114 . In fact , these long F - actin bundles were sufficient to propel the bacteria even when the dendritic - like F - actin core normally present within the structures was removed using reconstitution assays 114 . Thus , could L . monocytogenes selectively hijack actin crosslinkers , such as palladin , transgelin , nexilin and  - actinin 1 , to stiffen the comet / rocket tail ? Others have proposed that comet / rocket tail stiffness enables the bacteria to traverse the crowded intracellular environment , thus influencing their movement , and in turn , their cell - to - cell spreading 113 , 771 . In fact , when McGrath and colleagues ( 2003 ) increased the viscosity and thus drag load of actin - rich cytoplasmic extracts using methylcellulose , the comet / rocket tails compensated by nearly doubling in F - actin density 771 . I postulate that in the absence of this stiffness , the comet / rocket tails would become distorted , move at slower rates , and reach the cell surface at a lower frequency . Evidence for this comes from several studies that examined host cells depleted of comet / rocket tail F - actin crosslinking agents such as nexilin and transgelin 187 , 195 . In those studies , comet / rocket tails became shorter and bent in the absence of nexilin or transgelin 187 , 195 . I show similar findings in cells depleted of palladin . Dold and colleagues ( 1994 ) inhibition  - actinin 1 resulted in immobile L . monocytogenes bacteria 577 . I transfected host cells with the actin - binding and crosslinking deficient mutant variant of palladin . In those cells , I observed a ~ 2 . 4 fold decrease in bacterial motility rates . Although I did not examine the effect of decreased motility on the formation of membrane protrusions , others have . Sidhu and colleagues treatment of cells with the PI - 3 kinase inhibitor , LY294002 , slowed motile L . monocytogenes bacteria 772 . Importantly , they also observed a ~ 4 - fold reduction in number of membrane protrusions . This reduction in number of membrane protrusions was also observed by Dold and co - workers in their study inhibiting  - actinin 1 577 . Taken together , these observations highlight the comet / rocket tail as a robust actin - rich platform comprised of many F - actin stiffening agents ( such as palladin , nexilin and transgelin ) , which effectively transmits the bacteria to the host cell surface . Does this internal actin architecture of the comet / rocket tail also hold true at the membrane protrusion ? Interestingly , electron microscopic examination of the L . monocytogenes membrane protrusion reveals a drastic alteration in the F - actin network within the structures in comparison to the cytosolic comet / rocket tail 106 , 115 , 493 , 539 . Like the comet / rocket tail , a 260 branched Arp2 / 3 - based F - actin meshwork is observed proximal to the bacterial surface within the membrane protrusion 106 , 113 , 115 , 539 . However , the distal regions of the protrusions are comprised of long unbranched actin filament bundles 106 , 113 , 115 , 539 . This is accomplished by L . monocytogenes bacteria commandeering the formin class of actin nucleators when the membrane protrusion is initiated 534 . In infected host cells depleted of formin proteins , membrane protrusions are significantly shorter while comet / rocket tails remain unaltered 534 . Thus , actin assembly by these formins could help to explain the appearance of long unbranched filaments within the membrane protrusions . Cryo - electron microscopic examination of L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions by Jasnin and colleagues ( 2013 ) revealed that many of these long actin filaments are closely associated with the plasma membrane , while the core of the structures remains almost hollow 113 . This unusual hollowing of the membrane protrusion could be the result of the loss of actin crosslinkers , such as palladin , nexilin and  - actinin 1 , within the comet / rocket tail as it reaches the host cell surface 535 , 578 . In place of these actin crosslinkers , the bacteria seemingly rely on another set of host factors , such as the actin - binding proteins ezrin and  - actinin 4 , the membrane receptors CD44 and CD147 , as well as the protein folding enzyme CypA 249 . Collectively , this begs the question , why does L . monocytogenes need to induce a dramatic change in the F - actin network and the type of host factors found within membrane protrusions compared to comet / rocket tails ? To answer this , one must consider that unlike the comet / rocket tail , which simply propels L . monocytogenes bacteria within the host cytoplasm , the process of spreading between host cells requires that motile bacteria push against the host plasma membrane . The lipid bilayer , by its very nature , possesses various elastic characteristics , such as surface tension and resistance to deformation , which are often at play during normal cellular processes 773 – 781 . Thus , it may seem counterintuitive that the bacteria switch from a dense ( and stiff ) meshwork enriched with crosslinkers , such as palladin , nexilin and  - actinin 1 , to an F - actin network that also forms a hollow - like tube of long unbranched filaments within certain segments of the structures to deform the lipid bilayer during bacterial membrane protrusion formation . However , a growing body of evidence suggests that active actin - based propulsion , such that occurs during bacterial cytosolic motility , may not be the sole ( or major ) factor that drives cell - to - cell spreading ( see below ) . This is not to say the actin - based motility of the bacteria is unimportant ; rather , the main function of comet / rocket - based motility may in fact be to simply move the bacteria towards the host cell surface so 261 they can then initiate the protrusion forming mechanism . This could explain previous observations of fewer membrane protrusions when bacterial motility rates were slowed 577 , 772 . My findings and those of others hints that other , non - motility based mechanisms are at play during membrane protrusion formation and their eventual engulfment by the host cell . Possible mechanism are described below . Transitions from branched to parallel actin - based structures occur normally in cells . The lamellipodium at the leading edge of motile cells , like the comet / rocket tail , is rich in branched actin filaments whereas filopodial protrusions , which can emanate from the leading edge , are characterized by actin filament bundles that use parallel actin that is bundled along their length 23 – 25 , 83 , 113 , 147 , 782 – 785 . A model proposed by Hoffmann and Schafer also depicts fascin exchanging for palladin as filopodial F - actin bundles enter the branched actin - containing lamellipodium 786 . Despite a lack of evidence , I speculate that a similar transition is occurring within L . monocytogenes protrusions . With that said , the exact mechanism behind filopodium generation is currently debated and thus I can only speculate as to why L . monocytogenes might also hijack bundled actin 25 , 83 , 151 , 787 – 789 . Indeed , some of the first terminology used to describe L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions were “filopod” and “pseudopod” 115 , 521 , 732 , 772 , 790 , 791 . Like filopodia , the L . monocytogenes membrane protrusion extends outwards as a narrow projection from the cell surface and both structures are motile 142 , 539 . The presence of formin proteins ( and bundled F - actin ) is of course puzzling , but one possibility is they may serve to lengthen and stabilize the relatively thin membranous protrusive structures more efficiently than branched actin . Whether or not L . monocytogenes also sense and signal within their microenvironment remains an important question to be answered . Importantly , both filopodia and L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions rely on many of the same proteins for their proper formation . Ezrin , CD44 , formins , CD147 ,  - actinin 4 and cyclophilins are all crucial for the proper formation of filopodial structures and L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions 249 , 534 . Indeed , the appearance of collapsed and shorter membrane protrusions is also phenocopied in ezrin depleted cells at their filopodia ( and also microvilli ) 792 – 794 . Conversely , the absence of these membrane protrusion specific factors ( ezrin , CD44 , formins , CD147 ,  - actinin 4 and CypA ) at cytosolic comet / rocket tails , and the fact that comet / rocket tails maintain their normal morphology / function in cells inhibited of these proteins hints towards their selective role during membrane protrusion formation 249 , 534 . Whether or not other comet / rocket tail actin crosslinkers are also absent at the membrane 262 protrusions remains to be seen . Ultimately , we are only in the early stages of unraveling the mechanisms behind L . monocytogenes membrane protrusion formation and although my findings highlight new host factors that are vital at the structures , they also bring to light many fundamental questions that need to be answered including : 1 ) how do the membrane receptors CD44 and CD147 become clustered around membrane protrusions , 2 ) how are formin proteins and CypA selectively recruited within the membrane protrusion core , 3 ) what is the exact function of CypA within the protrusion core and 4 ) can L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions actively degrade interstitial matrix ? Historically it has long been thought that motile L . monocytogenes bacteria “push” into neighbouring cells using the L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions and that this governs their internalization and spreading from one cell to another . Upon closer examination of L . monocytogenes spreading events , a cup - like invagination is generated at the surface of the membrane protrusion - receiving cell . My finding of CD147 at the invagination membrane suggests that these structures might be endocytic given their overall morphology as well as the fact that CD147 can trigger endocytosis 335 , 346 , 795 – 800 . However , compared to conventional endocytic pits , the L . monocytogenes membrane invaginations are many fold larger than regular endosomes ( μm vs . nm ) . Yet there is evidence of the host endocytic machinery at micron - scaled structures : EPEC and S . flexneri commandeer clathrin and its associated proteins during actin pedestal formation and cell - to - cell spreading respectively 338 , 349 . Surprisingly , I found the caveolin endocytic machinery , as well as the clathrin interacting protein epsin - 1 , localized to the membrane invaginations induced as the protrusions projected into neighboring host cells . Depletion of caveolin - 1 or epsin - 1 perturbed bacterial cell - to - cell spreading suggesting these invaginations are actively internalizing the invading protrusion . I also reveal that isolated non - motile membrane protrusions which are in contact with the host cell surface induce the recruitment of caveolar endocytic components around the structures . Despite the recruitment of those proteins , those isolated protrusions did not enter the host cells . Consequently , an interplay between the endocytic and actin propulsive events are likely required for these large structures to enter neighbouring cells . Aside from the direct significance of caveolin for L . monocytogenes dissemination , the membrane invaginations now present an exciting model for researchers to study large scale endocytic events . A considerable amount of controversy exists in the field of caveolin endocytosis , mainly regarding the exact role of caveolae within cells . While caveolae can internalize 263 extracellular cargo normally in cell , I show here that caveolae indirectly permit the entry of large particles through their ability to collapse into the plasma membrane . Whether or not other bacterial pathogens usurp non - canonical functions of the caveolin endocytic machinery for their invasion or dissemination will be great interest for future investigations . 264 Chapter 9 . Future Directions Palladin In chapter 2 , I demonstrated that palladin can functionally compensate for the loss of the Arp2 / 3 complex during L . monocytogenes actin - based motility . This work follows up on the in vitro discovery of branched actin filaments when purified palladin and actin were co - incubated 206 . Taken together , one crucial question comes to mind , can palladin nucleate branched F - actin arrays normally in cells ? Furthermore , could these palladin - mediated F - actin arrays drive cellular motility ? A discovery such as this could significantly alter the current landscape in how cell biologists currently view actin - based motility given that the Arp2 / 3 complex , followed closely by the formin family of proteins , are considered the major engines driving cell migration both in vitro and in vivo . One way to examine this would be to utilize a highly motile immortalized cell line depleted of the Arp2 / 3 complex . A simple way to deplete the Arp2 / 3 complex would be to inhibit it using the potent inhibitor CK - 666 , as described in chapter 2 494 . Another potentially effective , but laborious approach , would be to ablate genomic sequences encoding the major Arp2 / 3 subunits ( Arp2 and Arp3 ) using CRISPR / Cas9 . Following this , one could examine cell motility rates of individual cells or groups of cells ( via a scratch assay ) , two - dimensionally ( i . e . on a glass coverslip ) , using real - time phase contrast or fluorescence microscopy . Importantly , these motility rates could then be compared to Arp2 / 3 depleted cells also overexpressing wild - type palladin . To examine the actin cytoskeleton within Arp2 / 3 depleted cells versus depleted cells overexpressing palladin , metal replica electron microscopy could be utilized as this method provides a high resolution and three - dimensional depiction of actin arrays versus convention transmission electron microscopy techniques 23 , 24 . Because cells generally do not migrate two - dimensionally in the body , it will also be crucial to examine the role of palladin during cellular migration in three - dimensional cell culture as this method better represents the microenvironment of living tissue . Interestingly , the literature describes several cancers in which palladin is highly upregulated 664 – 667 . Because these tumor cells are extremely motile , could palladin therefore be co - opted to produce additional F - actin branches to help drive cell migration ? Thus , I envision the use of confocal microscopy imaging of these three dimensionally cultured tumor cells , in 265 conjunction with perfusion of the 3D matrix itself with the Arp2 / 3 inhibitor , CK - 666 . If palladin does in fact promote cell migration via its actin nucleating activity , I postulate that these tumor cells would display high levels of motility even in the absence of functional Arp2 / 3 . Several other bacterial ( and viral ) pathogens , such as S . flexneri and Rickettsia rickettsii ( R . rickettsia ) generate actin comet / rocket tails for their intracellular motility 106 , 738 , 801 , 802 . Thus , it will also be important to find out whether or not these pathogens also hijack palladin during their actin - based motility . Importantly , the actin comet / rocket tails generated by R . rickettsia bacteria are well - known for containing abundant parallel F - actin arrays 106 , 801 . Thus , R . rickettsia comet / rocket tails could be utilized as a cell biological tool to understand the role of palladin at parallel F - actin - containing structures in the cell . Cyclophilin A and CD147 CypA and CD147 expression are crucial for maintaining the structural integrity of L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions ; however , the precise mechanism behind CypA - and CD147 - mediated protrusion stabilization remains unclear . Given that both proteins do not possess any known actin - binding domains or motifs , there most likely exists a missing host factor which links these proteins to the F - actin within the structures . A potential candidate to investigate at membrane protrusions is α - actinin 4 , as Maïssa and colleagues identified it as a new binding partner of CD147 during N . meningitidis infections 325 . Depletion of α - actinin 4 using siRNA will provide a quick and easy method to examine any morphological changes to membrane protrusions in the absence of α - actinin 4 . The formin family of proteins as well as the ERM protein , ezrin , are also crucial for membrane protrusion formation 249 . Therefore , it will be important to determine whether or not these proteins directly interact with CypA and / or CD147 . Because CypA is well known as a molecular chaperone , could CypA properly activate formins and / or ezrin at membrane protrusions ? CD147 induces the synthesis of matrix metalloproteinases ( MMPs ) , which degrade interstitial matrix 803 – 810 . Thus , it would be interesting to examine the presence of these MMPs at membrane protrusions during infection of host cells that are also adhered onto a matrix - like substrate given recent findings highlighting L . monocytogenes exit at the basal face of polarized epithelial cells 495 . 266 Caveolin - 1 My finding that caveolin - 1 , and caveolae as a whole , play a crucial role in the uptake of L . monocytogenes membrane protrusions adds further support for a non - canonical role of caveolin in large particle endocytosis 647 , 648 . While there exists some evidence in the field that caveolin could regulate phagocytosis ( the uptake of large particles such as dead / dying cell and pathogens ) , the precise function of caveolin during these processes remains unclear 647 , 648 . Importantly , whether or not other caveolar proteins are also involved in these large scale endocytic events remains unclear . Thus , L . monocytogenes membrane invaginations could represent a potential model to study caveolar components during large scale endocytosis . One of the major questions regarding the presence of caveolar proteins , as well as the clathrin - interacting protein epsin - 1 , at L . monocytogenes membrane invaginations is in what order do these proteins arrive at the structures ? Of course , it will also be useful to examine the order by which these proteins are shed from the eventual double - membraned vacuoles once the invaginations have undergone scission . The sequence of endocytic protein arrival ( and shedding ) from clathrin coated pits / vesicles is well - studied ; however , the same cannot be said of caveolae 326 – 329 , 333 , 350 , 430 , 811 , 812 . One way to accomplish this would be to utilize confocal ( or super resolution ) microscopy to live image membrane invagination forming cells that express fluorescently - tagged versions of the various invagination proteins described in chapter 3 . Specifically , each protein should be tracked starting from the initial contact of the membrane protrusion with the receiving cell surface and all the way through to the eventual scission of the invagination into a double - membraned vacuole . Clathrin endocytosis utilizes over 30 proteins . Therefore , although my findings in chapter 3 show a clear absence of clathrin , and the major clathrin adaptor protein , AP2 , at L . monocytogenes membrane invaginations , a full analysis of the remaining clathrin endocytic proteins should be carried out . Furthermore , eukaryotic cells also utilize several clathrin - and caveolin - independent micropinocytic mechanisms , such as those controlled by Arf6 , endophillin , the flotillins , and GRAF1 330 , 335 , 398 , 813 – 819 , 820 ( p6 ) . These proteins should also be examined ( as described in chapter 3 ) at L . monocytogenes invaginations in order to understand the full extent of host endocytic mechanisms at play during bacterial cell - to - cell spreading events . The identification of any of these other endocytic proteins at the 267 structures could provide crucial insight into the potential for endocytic mechanism cross - talk , as these pathways are generally considered to function independently of one another normally during endocytosis . 268 Chapter 10 . Conclusion In conclusion , my findings expand the current repertoire of host factors that are exploited during infections by actin - hijacking pathogens . My investigation of palladin , cyclophilin A , and CD147 during L . monocytogenes , EPEC , S . Typhimurium and S . flexneri infections , highlights key roles for these proteins at several well - known stages of the bacteria infectious cycle . In parallel to this , I exploited the bacterial infections , and the actin - rich structures they generate , as a useful cell biological tool in order to uncover new cellular functions for these host proteins . Lastly , my discovery that L . monocytogenes exploits host caveolin for efficient cell - to - cell spreading , answers the longstanding question of how membrane protrusions are engulfed by cells . As the host actin cytoskeleton and endocytic machinery are common targets of many human pathogens , these findings provide a way to help unravel some of the mechanisms underlying common microbe - host interactions . Furthermore , this work also represents another perspective by which to rethink some of the literature on actin cytoskeletal dynamics as well as caveolin - mediated endocytosis and to address some of the controversies within these fields . 269 References 1 . Semin Cell Dev Biol . 2011 ; 22 ( 1 ) : 39 - 47 . doi : 10 . 1016 / j . semcdb . 2010 . 09 . 002 335 Appendix : Supplementary Movies Movie 2 . 1 . Palladin and F - actin Colocalize throughout L . monocytogenes Motility mKate - LifeAct ( to visualize actin ) and GFP - palladin co - transfected Ptk2 cells were infected with wild type L . monocytogenes and visualized 8 hours post infection . GFP - palladin and actin are colocalized at stationary actin clouds and , subsequently , at comet tails during bacterial intracellular motility ( arrowheads ) . Elapsed time displayed in minutes and seconds . Scale bar , 10 µm . Movie 2 . 2 . Palladin Is Shed from Comet Tails during Listeriopod Formation Crop of Movie S1 showing GFP - palladin is shed from comet tails during listeriopod formation ( arrowheads ) . Elapsed time displayed in minutes and seconds . Scale bar , 5 µm . Movie 2 . 3 . L . monocytogenes Comet Tails Disintegrate in PalladinK15 / 18 / 51A - Expressing Cells mKate - LifeAct ( to visualize actin ) and GFP - palladinK15 / 18 / 51A co - transfected HeLa cells were infected with wild type L . monocytogenes and visualized 8 hours post infection . Comet tails ( arrowheads ) move slower and dramatically disintegrate at their distal ends into clumps ( full arrows ) during dynamic motility . Elapsed time displayed in minutes and seconds . Scale bar , 5 µm . Movie 2 . 4 . L . monocytogenes Comet Tails Are Thin and Tethered to Diffuse Actin Clouds in PalladinFPAA - Expressing Cells mKate - LifeAct ( to visualize actin ) and GFP - palladinFPAA co - transfected HeLa cells were infected with wild type L . monocytogenes and visualized 8 hours post infection . Bacteria form diffuse actin clouds ( full arrows ) that remain behind the bacteria during dynamic motility . Motile comet tails ( arrowheads ) remain attached to diffuse clouds at their distal ends , move slower as well as become progressively thinner as they move . Elapsed time displayed in minutes and seconds . Scale bar , 10 µm . Movie 2 . 5 . L . monocytogenes Comet Tails and Actin Clouds Disintegrate Immediately in the Presence of CK - 666 mKate - LifeAct ( to visualize actin ) transfected HeLa cells were infected with wild type L . monocytogenes and visualized 8 hours post infection . During imaging , culture media was replaced with media containing CK - 666 ( 100 µM ; indicated by text at top left ) and imaging was allowed to continue . Immediately upon treatment with CK - 666 , actin clouds ( full arrows ) disintegrate and motile comet tails halt to a complete stop and disassemble ( arrowheads ) . Elapsed time displayed in minutes and seconds . Scale bar , 10 µm . 336 Movie 2 . 6 . Palladin Overexpression Compensates for Arp2 / 3 Complex Defects during L . monocytogenes Motility mKate - LifeAct ( to visualize actin ) and GFP - palladin co - transfected HeLa cells were infected with wild type L . monocytogenes and visualized 8 hours post infection . During imaging , culture media was replaced with media containing CK - 666 ( 100 µM ; indicated by text at top left ) and imaging was allowed to continue . Upon treatment with CK - 666 , comet tails ( arrowhead ) continue to move unperturbed by functional inhibition of Arp2 / 3 complexes throughout the course of drug treatment . Elapsed time displayed in minutes and seconds . Scale bar , 10 µm . Movie 2 . 7 . Initiation of L . monocytogenes Motility is Unaffected by CK - 666 in Cells Overexpressing Palladin Crop of Movie S6 showing L . monocytogenes bacteria ( arrowheads ) are able to enter dynamic motility similarly to normal untreated cells even when the Arp2 / 3 complex is functionally inhibited . Elapsed time displayed in minutes and seconds . Scale bar , 5 µm . Movie 2 . 8 .
